    <dl>
           <dt>ha 1</dt>
           <dd><em>ha</em> the thirty-third and last consonant of the N&#x0101;gar&#x012b; alphabet (in P&#x0101;&#x1e47;ini's system belonging to the guttural class, and usually pronounced like the English <em>h</em> in <em>hard</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; it is not an original letter, but is mostly derived from an older <em>gh</em>, rarely from <em>dh</em> or <em>bh</em>)</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; hak&#x0101;ra </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;k&#x0101;ra</em> m. the letter or sound <em>ha</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MW">MW.</a></dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; hatva </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;tva</em> n. the state of the letter <em>ha</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a></dd>

           <dt>ha 2</dt>
           <dd><em>ha</em> (only <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#L">L.</a>), m. a form of &#x015a;iva or Bhairava (cf. <em>nakul&#x012b;7&#x015b;a</em>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; water </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a cipher (i.e. the arithmetical figure which symbolizes o) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; meditation, auspiciousness </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sky, heaven, paradise </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; blood </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; dying </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; fear </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; knowledge </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the moon </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; Vish&#x1e47;u </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; war, battle </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; horripilation </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a horse </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; pride </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a physician </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; cause, motive </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; = <em>p&#x0101;pa-hara&#x1e47;a</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; = <em>sakopa-v&#x0101;ra&#x1e47;a</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; = <em>&#x015b;u&#x1e63;ka</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (also <em>&#x0101;</em> f.) laughter </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (<em>&#x0101;</em>), f. coition </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a lute (<em>am</em>), n. the Supreme Spirit </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; pleasure, delight </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a weapon </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the sparkling of a gem </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; calling, calling to the sound of a lute </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (ind.) = <em>aham</em> (?), IndSt </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; mfn. mad, drunk</dd>

           <dt>ha 3</dt>
           <dd><em>ha</em> ind. (prob. orig. identical with 2. <em>gha</em>, and used as a particle for emphasizing a preceding word, esp. if it begins a sentence closely connected with another </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; very frequent in the Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;as and S&#x016b;tras, and often translatable by) indeed, assuredly, verily, of course, then &amp;c. (often with other particles, e.g. with <em>tv eva</em>, <em>u</em>, <em>sma</em>, <em>vai</em> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>na ha</em>, 'not indeed' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; also with interrogatives and relatives, e.g. <em>yad dha</em>, 'when indeed' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>kad dha</em>, 'what then?' sometimes with impf. or pf. [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#cf">cf.</a> P&#x0101;&#x1e47;. 3-2, 116] </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in later language very commonly used as a mere expletive, esp. at the end of a verse) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c</dd>

           <dt>ha 4</dt>
           <dd><em>ha</em> mf(<em>&#x0101;</em>)n. (fr. &#x221a;<em>han</em>) killing, destroying, removing (only ifc </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; See <em>ar&#x0101;ti-</em>, <em>v&#x1e5b;tra-</em>, <em>&#x015b;atruha</em> &amp;c.)</dd>

           <dt>ha 5</dt>
           <dd><em>ha</em> mf(<em>&#x0101;</em>)n. (fr. &#x221a;3. <em>h&#x0101;</em>) abandoning, deserting, avoiding (ifc </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; See <em>an-oka-</em> and <em>v&#x0101;p&#x012b;-ha</em>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (<em>&#x0101;</em>), f. abandonment, desertion <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#L">L.</a></dd>

           <dt>ha&#x1e43;sa 1</dt>
           <dd><em>ha&#x1e43;s&#x00e1;</em> m. (ifc. f. <em>&#x0101;</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; accord. to <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#U&#x1e47;">U&#x1e47;.</a> iii, 62 fr. &#x221a;1. <em>han</em>, 'to go?') a goose, gander, swan, flamingo (or other aquatic bird, considered as a bird of passage </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sometimes a mere poetical or mythical bird, said in <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> to be able to separate Soma from water, when these two fluids are mixed, and in later literature, milk from water when these two are mixed </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; also forming in <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> the vehicle of the A&#x015b;vins, and in later lit&#x1e6d;literature that of Brahm&#x0101; </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; ifc. also = 'best or chief among') <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; sometimes 'the Universal Soul or Supreme Spirit', identified with Vir&#x0101;j, N&#x0101;r&#x0101;ya&#x1e47;a, Vish&#x1e47;u, &#x015a;iva, K&#x0101;ma, and the Sun </dd>

           <dt>&#x226b; hanumat </dt>
           <dd><em>hanu-mat</em> m. 'having (large) jaws', N. of a monkey-chief (one of the most celebrated of a host of semi-divine monkey-like beings, who, according to <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> i, 16, were created to become the allies of R&#x0101;ma-candra in his war with R&#x0101;va&#x1e47;a </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; Hanumat was held to be a son of Pavana or M&#x0101;ruta, 'the Wind' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; and is fabled to have assumed any form at will, wielded rocks, removed mountains, mounted the air, seized the clouds, and rivalled Garu&#x1e0d;a in swiftness of flight </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; according to other legends, Hanumat was son of &#x015a;iva </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; his mother's name was A&#x00f1;jan&#x0101;, q.v </dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; m. N. of the 28th king of the solar dynasty in the Tret&#x0101; age (he was son of Tri-&#x015b;a&#x1e45;ku, and was celebrated for his piety </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; accord. to the M&#x0101;rka&#x1e47;&#x1e0d;eya-Pur&#x0101;&#x1e47;a he gave up his country, his wife and his son, and finally himself, to satisfy the demands of Vi&#x015b;v&#x0101;mitra </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; after enduring incredible sufferings, he won the pity of the gods and was raised with his subjects to heaven: accord. to <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> ii, 489 &amp;c., his performance of the R&#x0101;ja-s&#x016b;ya sacrifice was the cause of his elevation, and in the Aitareya-Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a quite another legend is told about him, See under <em>&#x015b;una&#x1e25;&#x015b;epa</em>, p. 1082, col. 3: in later legends Hari-&#x015b;candra is represented as insidiously induced by N&#x0101;rada to relate his actions with unbecoming pride, whereupon he was degraded from Svarga, one stage at each sentence, till stopping in time and doing homage to the gods he was fixed with his capital in mid-air <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p1291-1"></a>[Page 1291, Column 1]</font> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; his aerial city is popularly believed to be still visible in the skies at particular times </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; cf. <em>saubha</em>) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Br">Br.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MaitrUp">MaitrUp.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; N. of various authors &amp;c. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Inscr">Inscr.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Cat">Cat.</a>: m. or n. (?) N. of a place <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Cat">Cat.</a> </dd>

           <dt>hi 2</dt>
           <dd><em>h&#x00ed;</em> ind. (used as a particle [cf. <em>ha</em> and <em>gha</em>] and usually denoting) for, because, on account of (never standing first in a sentence, but generally after the first word and used enclitically, sometimes after pronouns </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; e.g. <em>s&#x00e1;rvo h&#x00ed; p&#x1e5b;&#x0301;tan&#x0101; jig&#x012b;&#x1e63;ati</em>, 'for everybody wishes to win battles' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>bkav&#x0101;n hi pram&#x0101;&#x1e47;am</em>, 'for your honour is the authority' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>tah&#x0101; hi</em>, 'for example', 'accordingly' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>n&#x00e1; h&#x00ed;</em> or <em>nah&#x012b;&#x0341;</em>', for not', 'not at all') <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; just, pray, do (with an Impv. or Pot. emphatically </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sometimes with Indic., e. g. <em>pasy&#x0101;mo hi</em>, 'we will just see') <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; indeed, assuredly, surely, of course, certainly (<em>h&#x00ed; va&#x00ed;</em>, 'most assuredly' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>hi-tu</em> or <em>hi-punar</em>, 'indeed-but' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; often a mere expletive, esp. to avoid a hiatus, sometimes repeated in the same sentence </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>hi</em> is also said to be an interjection of 'envy', 'contempt', 'hurry' &amp;c.) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a></dd>
